Various Essays

Tidbits 233

— (Fang Shujun)

"In the world, there are only things that should not be done, there are absolutely no things that cannot be done." Therefore, a person must have a clear goal and a firm ambition. The more dangerous the time, the more firm our will must be. We must seek the true joy of life from the midst of hard work, display the spirit of hard work, break through difficulties and obstacles, and achieve the ultimate goal.

Wilhelm II said: "The more difficult, the more firm." If we can have this spirit of hard work, then everything will be solved easily. Even if there are thousands of difficulties and hardships, we can embrace the belief that "all troubles are to help me train my mind, all dangers are to help me train my courage." Then there is no reason not to be free and content, and there is nothing to hinder us. This is also ironclad proof that "danger is our opportunity to strengthen ourselves."

The road of life is like climbing stairs. Each step is more difficult than the last. If we do not work hard, it will be difficult to reach the top. Therefore, "failure for want of a single basketful" is the most heartbreaking thing.

The most pitiful person in the world is a child without a mother, but the most hopeful person is also a child without a mother. Therefore, a person who can rise up from hardship is bound to be a noble person who is good at controlling the environment.

"Slow" 234

— Sleeping Buddha

The underdevelopment of Chinese education is undeniable, but the emphasis on this 'slow' education is ubiquitous. Therefore, both the government and the public, men and women, young and old, treat this 'slow' word as the golden rule for establishing oneself and dealing with the world. Even now, they are still stagnating in a 'slow' state, and there is a tendency to make it even worse now.

For example, when a child is learning to walk, adults are always warning him to "walk slowly" and "run slowly." Of course, this is for the child's safety to avoid the danger of tripping. But this 'slow' kind of lesson has been deeply imprinted in the child's mind. Usually, when saying goodbye to a relative or friend, or when seeing a guest out, the first and last words are always "walk slowly" and "go slowly." This is naturally also well-intentioned, for fear that the other person is too tired. Furthermore, in old novels or dramas, as well as in ordinary oral communication, one can always hear the tone of "wait a minute" and "come slowly." When you hear this tone, you can imagine how leisurely they are. In addition, the Ningbo people's 'Chai Ji Sha,' our southern people's 'slow'! 'Slow!' 'Eat slowly!' 'Do it slowly!' are also just common, well-meaning admonitions. ... What is even more valuable is that there are also many indications of 'slow' in the holy books and virtuous biographies: 'Walk slowly and you will grow taller,' then people will praise you for knowing politeness; but if you are 'zealous for profit,' then you will honestly be labeled as a follower of Zhi (a famous robber). (The author is not against the holy teachings, but because later people often misunderstand the holy books and use them inappropriately). Regarding this kind of slow education, in the family, in society, and in books, because it is so serious and common, it will naturally cultivate the Chinese person's slow nature, slow habits, and traditionally be a slow follower, only believing in slow and being content with slow, and comfortable with slow.

In that case, it is no wonder that everything before us--from national affairs to personal studies--must be stranded in 'slowly,' I'm just afraid that one day, people will come to interfere with your slowness--ah! Really, who dares to believe that there won't be such a day--the coming of the end of slowness.

Lines 235

— Zhou Xian

Every picture, what cannot be missed, is a number of lines that can be analyzed, curved, straight, thick, and thin.

For example, a city's framework consists of large buildings with straight lines. However, within these large buildings with straight lines, several curved lines of roadside trees must be planted to moderate the monotonous impression reflected in human vision. Therefore, very few people stroll along the main roads and four main roads. Conversely, in places like Avenue Joffre and Yuyuan Road, there are plenty of women holding men's arms, and men with their arms around women's waists, talking, laughing, and walking. This is because in Avenue Joffre and Yuyuan Road, there are three-dimensional buildings and rural gardens. In the same picture, there are straight lines and curved lines, thick lines and thin lines, unlike what is seen in main roads and four main roads, which are entirely like cabinets, chests, boxes, and caskets, seemingly a geometrical picture.

Indeed, every beautiful picture inevitably needs curves, but at the same time, it also needs straight lines; inevitably needs thin lines, but at the same time, it also needs thick lines. Therefore, in a desolate mountain, a pagoda composed of straight lines must be placed. In scenic spots, there are always several temples composed of straight lines. Above a river composed of curves, a stone slab bridge composed of straight lines must be built. In scenic areas that can attract tourists, if one or two three-dimensional grand hotels are hidden in the shade of green and sparse red mountain forests, it will surely give tourists an indescribable sense of pleasure. Just as in a city entirely composed of straight lines, several streamlined cars are gliding, making the dull gaze feel a lot of stimulation.

Therefore, in this day and age, gentlemen with square shoulders must appreciate women with curves, so that they can form a beautiful picture composed of curves and straight lines. At the same time, the face of every modern woman must also be researched by beauty experts to determine which part should be transformed into a straight line and which part should be transformed into a curve, so that they can be harmonious. Look, even these small eyebrows, some are straight, some are curved. For facial beauty, the first condition is naturally to pay attention to whether the interweaving of straight lines, curved lines, thick lines, and thin lines is harmonious.

Swapping the Nest for a Phoenix 236

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter 2: Fragrant Grasses and Beautiful Women, Gentle Waves Gently Entrust; Small Building, Bright Moon, Good Dreams Newly Warm

Guoqi took a look, then put his hands behind his back and slowly walked out of the pavilion. The man selling agate stones was calling from behind: "Sir, don't you want these stones? I have better ones here, I'll sell them to you cheaply. Our stones here are much cheaper than those at the temple." Guoqi turned his head and shook his head twice to indicate that he didn't want them. In this turning of the head, he saw that the girl was looking north towards the pavilion. Although they didn't know who each other was, as soon as their eyes met, they felt like the best of friends. Moreover, he had just said that the fragrant grasses were at the edge of the world, and that the spring scenery belonged to young people. This further showed that she had some ink in her belly, and was not an ordinary beauty. It was right to regard her as a plum blossom or an orchid. Thinking like this in his heart, he didn't dare to look at her, so he raised his head and looked at the clouds in the sky, the tiles of the pavilion, and even the acorns holding the tiles of the pavilion, which seemed to have some artistic meaning and were worth studying. Accidentally lowering his head to look straight ahead, he saw her admiring the scenery in front of the mountain, intentionally or unintentionally looking at him. Guoqi also thought that she was a lady, still very generous, and did not feel any awkwardness because they had met on the street. He, as a man, was being coy after seeing her, so he should loosen up a bit. So he struck up a conversation with the man selling agate stones and said with a smile: "You get these stones on this mountain very easily, and you still want to sell them for two copper coins apiece, that's too expensive." The vendor said with a smile: "Sir, although there are stones on the mountain, it's not easy to find good ones." As Guoqi walked towards the stall, the girl, along with two young women, also headed towards the stall. He suddenly said: "Sisters-in-law, do you think these agate stones come from this mountain? Actually, these stones are all collected from several counties near Nanjing. Although there are small stones everywhere on this mountain, there are very few good ones. Only after a heavy rain washes away the mountain soil will many stones be exposed, and then you can pick out a few good ones." As he spoke to his sisters-in-law, he looked around the pavilion. He was very generous and looked towards Guoqi's side. If you said that he was intentionally looking at people, his eyes were not specifically fixed on people. If you said that he was not looking at people, his eyes turned very flexibly towards this side. Protecting people felt a kind of indescribable pleasure. But he only paid attention to this side for a moment at the stone stall. Then he heard the young woman say "Let's go," and the three of them left the pavilion. When he left, his steps were slower than usual. He went from being in the front to being in the back, and he separated from the two sisters-in-law by a large distance. He looked back at the pavilion after every few steps until the corner at the foot of the mountain disappeared, and he could no longer see him looking back. (59)

Where the Travels Lead

Random Notes from a European Journey (Part 2) 237

— Zhu Xuefan

As for commerce, since the price of rubber fell, overseas Chinese merchants engaged in this business suffered miserably. Most of the rubber plantations fell into the hands of foreigners, and the impact on commerce was significant and substantial. Moreover, in recent years, the British have been monitoring overseas Chinese merchants engaged in rubber business quite strictly, and imposing various illegal and unfair restrictions, such as stipulating that Chinese cannot purchase real estate in certain areas, etc. And our overseas Chinese compatriots are passionate about patriotism, and deeply hope that the country is stable and strives for self-improvement, so that overseas Chinese merchants will not be insulted by others again. Most of the goods sold in the market are Japanese goods, or they are clearly labeled as British goods, but in fact, they are disguised. At that time, because the weather was very hot, I intended to buy a short-sleeved shirt produced by the Sanyou Industrial Society. However, there was only one Qiaoxing National Goods Company in the area, and I could not find any Sanyou products. Moreover, the goods displayed by the company were mixed and uneven. I asked why there were so many domestic national goods, why not order and sell them in batches from major domestic companies? According to the staff in the store, the price of national goods was too high, no one would buy them, and they would inevitably lose money. From this, it can be seen that the inability of national goods to develop abroad has its reasons. Moreover, although there are many overseas Chinese, there is no concrete organization. There are only associations such as guilds or hometown associations. The research institutions on how to develop the economy, commerce, and the entire overseas Chinese cause are still lacking, which is very worrying.

Overseas Chinese are divided into two factions: "Overseas Students" and "Foreign River." Overseas Chinese from Foreign River are proficient in the local language, while Overseas Student overseas Chinese only receive education from schools run by the British and do not learn the national language. Last year, due to living conditions, disputes unfortunately occurred. However, the Overseas Student overseas Chinese now know that only receiving English education is not enough to make a living in society, and they have set up a remedial national language school to remedy this, which is a good phenomenon. As for the overall education of overseas Chinese, it is still not universal. Although there are more than 300 primary schools, there is only one overseas Chinese male middle school and four female middle schools. Moreover, educational administration is often subject to various restrictions by the British, such as middle school principals and teachers must be approved by the British before they can be appointed, and the same is true for primary schools. Textbooks are also subject to British interference. To put it bluntly, it is nothing more than the enslavement education policy implemented by the British. Therefore, overseas Chinese who are rich in patriotism, within the scope of economic possibility, would rather send their children to study in the country to avoid being anesthetized by the British education policy. I believe that Jinan University in Zhenru, Shanghai, was established to educate the children of overseas Chinese. The school authorities should earnestly teach and pay attention to the special education on how to develop the economy, career, and trade of overseas Chinese in Nanyang, in order to cultivate talents and cultivate new soldiers of overseas Chinese merchants, so that what they have learned can be used, so as not to disappoint the hopes of our overseas Chinese.

Overseas Chinese have always been known for their ability to endure hardship and hard work, but there are also those who are addicted to smoking and gambling. Although the British authorities claim to prohibit it, in fact, they indulge in it in many ways. If the British authorities' tobacco tax revenue is used as a sacrifice, it will be clear. The most tobacco tax revenue was 31 million per year. In 1931, it was reduced to 6 million, and in the previous year, it increased to 8 million. In 1933, registration was once started, and the number of smokers reached 59,000. This year, the registration has been reduced to more than 26,400. On the surface, it seems to have been reduced by half, but according to those familiar with the situation, the number of smokers is more than 100,000.

Singapore is the British military base in the Pacific. The Second World War is about to break out. All countries are engaged in the expansion of armaments. The British have built a large naval port in Singapore, and foreigners are not allowed to enter. There is also a large-scale airport, which is also under construction. The British barracks are stationed in dense forests, and the preparation for defense is strict.

——25, 5, 2. Sailing on the Columbia.

The Zhong Kui of the Japanese Dragon Boat Festival 238

— Ji Yun

The Dragon Boat Festival is a solar term in the Chinese lunar calendar, but it has also been copied by Japan and changed to May 5th in the Gregorian calendar. After Japan abolished the Chinese lunar calendar, it followed the lunar calendar for all solar terms. Therefore, it is difficult to taste the loquat, which is necessary for the Chinese Dragon Boat Festival, in the Gregorian calendar. The Japanese do not have any activities during the Dragon Boat Festival. What they value most are temple fair days and various national memorial days.

In May, the Japanese hang cloth carp and windmills on bamboo poles, I don't know what it means. The carp is empty, and the wind enters the belly from the fish's mouth, and the belly swells up. Fluttering in the wind, it looks like jumping and swimming. Around May, the sky is the world of kites, mid-May is the world of carp, and after June, it is time to watch the Japanese fireworks.

The Japanese call clay dolls and foreign dolls as "human figures". What is popular in May is "warrior dolls". There are portraits of their Emperor Jinmu, wearing embroidered robes, black court boots, five strands of long beard, and unshaven hair. Some have two tufts on the left and right, and some tie their hair on top, completely in the style of ancient Chinese people. And with feathers inserted in the back, and a Japanese sword at the waist, it is even more the style of an ancient general. However, the left hand holds a long staff, with an old eagle coiled on top. On the right side of Emperor Jinmu, there must be a portrait of Zhong Kui, who is also worshiped by the Japanese. Unexpectedly, Zhong Kui, who is unattended to during the Dragon Boat Festival in our country, is very popular in Japan, and Sino-Japanese friendship is officially implemented.

When Zhong Jinshi went to Japan, it is probably not easy to investigate. Moreover, the face of Heitan Tuan has turned into a purplish brown color in Japan. But he still wears a pointed gauze hat on his head, and wears an embroidered python robe, not a red robe, like their Emperor Jinmu. His face is full of beard, and he holds a long sword, which is very majestic. Behind the two human figures, there is a row of shelves with knives, guns, and flags, and their portraits are also painted on the flags. In addition, there are bronze drums, bows, arrows, and various decorations. In front of the human figure, there is a set of Japanese armor, sitting on the animal skin, like our country's tiger skin treasure seat. The full set of human figures costs more than 30 yuan, and it may be difficult to buy unless they are from the upper middle class.

Around the time of the Dragon Boat Festival, Zhong Kui's vertical scroll will be hung in the living room. It is completely painted like a human figure, and it is not a black face. There are no bats and five ghosts next to it, it is extremely cold. When talking to the Japanese about Zhong Jinshi, they have seen him in Japan since they were young, and they no longer know that he is Chinese. Even our Chinese students, when they see this red-faced human figure, will not recognize that it is Zhong Jinshi, a pure domestic product of our country.

On the Dragon Boat Festival, reed leaves and mugwort are hung on the door. Several herbs are also put in the water in the bathhouse, which is the same as in our country. The fruit shop sells slender pen zongzi, just like in the country. Maybe there are many similar customs in the hometown.

Unofficial Biography of Master Wang 239

— Shi Jiu

Master Wang was a Xiucai during the Qing Dynasty and had sat for the provincial exams, and had been recommended for his papers. Master Wang was a landlord in his village, owning hundreds of acres of land. In the eyes of the villagers, Master Wang was a remarkable figure because he had studied the books of sages.

There was a teahouse in the town, which was Master Wang's office. He occupied a table alone all day long, sitting there and talking loudly: either saying that the donations and taxes were too harsh, or saying that people's hearts were not as good as before. He splattered saliva and spat phlegm everywhere. He yearned for the prosperity of the Tang, Yu, and Xia Dynasties. He hated the transformation of Xia by using barbarians. He had no hobbies and liked to smoke pi si but hated cigarettes. He scolded foreign goods, even though the teapot had been changed to a thermos bottle and the nail boots had been changed to rubber galoshes. Master Wang had a high reputation in the village, so everyone looked up to him. He would settle family disputes and money disputes. His words were more effective than the judgments in the court because he could, based on the classics of sages and the laws of the Qing Dynasty, make people dare not disobey him. He could also write lawsuits for others, and the reward was determined according to the size of the matter, although he could not be said to be a litigation broker.

Master Wang's treatment of people was very measured: he had one kind of expression for the tax collection committee members, another kind of face for the village police or village chiefs, and another kind of demeanor for tenant farmers and those who asked him for help. Master Wang walked in a very steady manner, quite like the style of an official in the Qing Dynasty; therefore, when the children in the village jumped around, their parents would reprimand them, "You have to learn from Master Wang!" Master Wang often took a small boat to the city. This was not because the steamer used barbarians to change Xia, but because the boat was cheaper; and when he walked into the boat, who would dare not give up a seat and respect him with a "Master".

Comment: "Master Wang, things are rare; although not expensive, enough to sigh"!

Two Red Peaches (Part 2) 240

— Fan Shouyuan

Here, I have to add a sentence; I wrote about composing lectures late at night, teaching and attending classes during the day, and other detailed matters before the onset of the disease. Isn't it too cumbersome? Actually, it is not. These trivial matters are often related to the occurrence of the disease and the degree of severity after it occurs. The occurrence of a disease must have its cause and effect. The so-called cause is the cause of the disease. In general, the causes of diseases are nothing more than: one is the cause of the disease itself, and the other is the cause of the human body environment. We can call this environmental cause its inducing cause. For example, dysentery and typhoid fever, their cause is dysentery bacteria and typhoid bacteria; but just relying on typhoid and dysentery bacteria is often not necessarily able to make everyone who has eaten it get sick, it must also have the help of the second environmental cause to be reliable. For example, sometimes after eating at the same table, someone develops dysentery and typhoid fever, and the rest are fine. What's the reason? I think: perhaps it is because the person who developed the disease had an inducing environmental cause, such as indigestion, lack of stomach acid, or inflammation of the stomach and intestines. These are all inducing causes. So once you eat typhoid bacteria and dysentery bacteria, you will develop typhoid fever and dysentery. What about the rest? Although they may have also eaten pathogens (bacteria), they do not develop the disease because there is no second inducing cause. Just like my attack of tonsillitis, if I hadn't stayed up late to compose lectures that night, and I wouldn't have had to force myself to attend classes the next day, this problem wouldn't have occurred. I dare not say that; but the time of occurrence and the severity of the disease might have been lighter, the time might have been shortened a little, and the body temperature might not have been so high. These are all very possible. But my attack of pure "red peaches" was really quite serious, and the time was quite long, so when I wrote the process, I also wrote some minor things that happened before the disease and had a causal relationship with the disease itself.

Perhaps someone will ask: You are a doctor yourself, a little tonsillitis, which is not a big disease, how can you let it develop so severely? Don't you use medicine, don't you treat it?

Medicine, how can I not use medicine and not treat it!

Speaking of diagnosing and treating diseases, I have to take the opportunity to talk about the psychological concepts of ordinary people and us doctors, what are the differences in medicine.

Indeed, our doctors' psychology for diagnosing diseases and our concepts for medicine are quite different from those of ordinary people: ordinary people's concepts for diagnosing diseases always think that doctors can see clearly at a glance, and after one examination, they can give an accurate diagnosis of what disease it is. Doctors' skills surpass Zhang Tianshi, and doctors' eyes are microscopes! As for medication, needless to say what medicine to use for what disease, it is only right and proper that it is not a cure, but it must reduce the disease after taking the medicine. Conversely, doctors' diagnosis of diseases and use of medicines are not so simple. There are certainly many diseases that are easily diagnosed and can be diagnosed and known what disease it is after one examination, and it is common; it is not uncommon to examine for ten or eight days, but the diagnosis is still vague and inexplicable. When it comes to medication, it is of course reasonable to only wait during the diagnostic period without special symptomatic drugs. Even after the diagnosis is clear and the condition is clear, it is often not necessary to use any drugs for treatment, and it is not unreasonable treatment. Because the treatment of diseases does not rely solely on drugs. When medicine is needed, the function of the medicine is seen after application. When medicine is not needed, it is not appropriate to use medicine: excessive use of drugs, or the skin may violate the sick body. Although this is off topic, it may be a little helpful for people who do not understand the correct concept of medicine diagnosis and treatment.

School Health Education (Part 2) 241

— Shao Xiangyi’s lecture, Li Lingdong’s notes

2. Adapt to circumstances can be divided into age differences and environmental differences. Because of different ages, the needs are also different. The psychological needs of five- or six-year-old children and thirteen- or fourteen-year-old children are obviously different. For environmental differences, attention should be paid to the different grades of rich and poor, and the strength of economic ability, and appropriate guidance should be given. This is something that those who study health education must know.

3. Use examples for citation This is the most powerful, practical, and effective method. For example, citing the pain of XX being sick and the death of XX due to illness, in the minds of every child, witnessing the tragic situation and hearing the truth, there is an urgent anxiety of terror, so using examples for citation, supplemented by appropriate explanations, the effect will be great.

4. Proceed in an orderly manner There are different differences in the academic abilities of high-grade and low-grade children, so we must first impart basic hygiene knowledge, and then gradually deepen it. Otherwise, if high-grade children are taught at a low-grade level, it will make them lack interest in hygiene.

5. It must be related to social problems Generally, people think that hygiene is a personal matter. This idea is really wrong, because individuals cannot be independent from society. If the public does not pay attention to hygiene, even if individuals can pay attention to hygiene, they will eventually suffer in an unhygienic environment. For example, poor tap water equipment can spread diseases through drinking water. It can be seen that paying attention to hygiene, in addition to personal attention, must also pay attention to public health undertakings related to individuals.

III Methods of Implementing Health Education

1. Performance Select stimulating scripts and movies containing health education, so that children can learn lessons and know the effects.

2. Storytelling Select various stories related to hygiene, so that children can learn to have aspirations and imitate them through admiration and worship.

3. Chinese Painting Lanterns Collect and produce hygiene drawings and lanterns, and post them in the passages of the school. The lanterns are shown, so that they can be eye-catching and stimulate children's attention to hygiene.

4. Text Use stimulating hygienic sentences and hygienic books and newspapers, arranged in various places in the school.

5. Talk Show Put forward opinions on health education and hygienic knowledge.

6. Competition Hold hygiene speech contests, hygiene drawing contests, hygiene performance contests, hygiene labor contests, hygiene stories, hygiene text various competitions, etc.

7. Visit Visit various medical institutions, health institutions, and institutions related to health undertakings.

8. Practice Practice various courses on the spot, so that theory and practice are equally important.

9. Exam

IV Content of Health Education Materials

1. Knowledge of anatomical life burying shall clarify the structure and function of each system and organ of the human body "skeleton", "muscle", "digestion", "circulation", "breathing", "excretion", and "sensation".

2. Knowledge of medicine and hygiene should include the causes, symptoms, and general treatment methods of various diseases, and the general knowledge of personal hygiene and public hygiene, such as the prevention of infectious diseases, the improvement of environmental hygiene, the general application of school hygiene, the attention to safety hygiene, and the rules of daily personal hygiene.

3. Knowledge of biology, chemistry and physics such as the physical and chemical phenomena of food digestion, as well as the origin of human beings, the law of heredity, etc. (End)

Common Knowledge of Diseases: Questions and Answers 242

— Cheng Hanzhang

(82) Chickenpox

(Question) What is Chickenpox?

(Answer) Chickenpox is an acute infectious disease of unknown etiology. It mostly affects children. The body develops a type of pox, similar to smallpox, but the content of the pox is transparent.

(Question) What is the Western name for Chickenpox?

(Answer) Chickenpox, in German is called Wasserpocken or Windpocken, in Latin it is Varicella, and in English it is Chickenpox.

(Question) How is Chickenpox spread?

(Answer) Although the etiology of chickenpox is unknown, it is likely present in the contents of the vesicles; it is transmitted through contact between patients and healthy individuals. Children under ten years old are more susceptible, and it is rare in adults.

(Question) After infection, how many days does it take to develop the disease?

(Answer) It takes a latent period of thirteen to seventeen days after infection for the disease to develop.

(Question) What are the conditions when the disease develops?

(Answer) It usually begins with a moderate fever, followed by the appearance of rashes, accompanied by itching. The rashes appear as small, bead-like, red, round lesions, which soon become blisters, mainly appearing on the trunk; they are less common on the face and limbs. The center of the blisters is slightly depressed; the contents are colorless and transparent fluid, sometimes turbid.

(Question) What is the condition of the fever?

(Answer) The fever is not very high, and it decreases on the second day of the illness, returning to normal temperature by the third or fourth day.

(Question) What happens to the rashes later on?

(Answer) Later, the blisters dry up and fall off within one to two weeks without leaving any scars.

(Question) Besides the skin rash, are there any other parts where rashes develop in chickenpox?

(Answer) Rashes can also develop on the tongue, head, throat, conjunctiva, etc.

(Question) What diseases are commonly associated with chickenpox?

(Answer) The most common is acute hemorrhagic brachial neuritis, which occurs on the fourth or fifth day of the illness; other associated conditions include arthritis, cellulitis, abscess, erysipelas, and gangrene.

(Question) How is chickenpox diagnosed?

(Answer) Diagnosis is easy based on the sudden onset of fever and rash in children, followed by papules and blisters.

(Question) What is the prognosis of this disease?

(Answer) It is good; however, the hemorrhagic form is not good.

(Question) How is chickenpox treated?

(Answer) Rest in bed is necessary, and urine should be checked frequently. If proteins are found, treatment should focus on the kidneys. For the skin rash, calamine lotion or talcum powder can be applied to relieve itching, allowing it to run its natural course.

Venereal Disease in a Girls' School: Mr. Li Ting'an's Original Speech 243

— Newspaper Reports Slightly Differ

Since Mr. Li Ting'an, Director of the Municipal Health Bureau, gave a speech at the Prophylactic Venereology Conference initiated by the Chinese Medical Association, various newspapers have published reports of Mr. Li's speech, stating that 30% of the students in a certain girls' middle school in Shanghai were suffering from syphilis. The Chinese Medical Association points out that this record is slightly different from Mr. Li's original speech in order to avoid misunderstandings? The association hereby publishes the original text of Mr. Li's speech as follows: "Mr. Li said that to the best of his knowledge, a certain girls' school in Shanghai once recruited new students. A total of fifty-two people applied, and eighteen were admitted after the examination. Among these eighteen people, after performing the Wassermann blood test, four tested positive for syphilis, accounting for more than 22% of the total. This situation is indeed occasional. However, the age of the applicants at that time was older than usual, and many were already married, so it cannot be compared with other girls' schools."

Medicinal Plants of Domestic Origin (Continued) 244

— Zhou Mengbai

Uncaria rhynchophylla, Matsum.

(Plant) Naturally grows in warm regions, a deciduous vine. Two hooked spines grow from the leaf axils to climb on other objects. Leaves are opposite, petiolate, oblong-ovate, acuminate, and white on the reverse side. Small yellow funnel-shaped flowers bloom in summer. The fruit is broadly elliptical.

(Crude Drug) Uncaria hooks, the Rhynchophylla, are collected from its hooks and the connecting stem. The hooks are roughly opposite along the main axis, usually in the shape of a developed fishhook, the large ones being 1 cm and the width 8 mm. The surface is reddish-brown or dark brown, and the texture is hard. The taste is bitter, with astringency.

(Ingredients) The leaves and hooks contain Rhynchophylline, a crystalline alkaloid. Its molecular formula is C22H28N2O4 or C21H26N2O4.

(Pharmacology) A small amount of Rhynchophylline can stimulate the respiratory center, and it has the same effect on the internal organs of frogs as Digitalis. Blood pressure is significantly reduced by Rhynchophylline, and peripheral blood vessels dilate. Intravenous injection in rabbits shows obvious dyspnea and motor paralysis as general symptoms. If the lethal dose is reached, death occurs due to respiratory paralysis. The minimum lethal dose for a rabbit weighing 1,000 grams is 35-40 mg by intravenous injection, and 0.03 grams by subcutaneous injection, which only shows signs of rapid breathing.

(Medicinal Use) According to ancient texts, Uncaria hooks can treat infantile convulsions, headaches, and dizziness in adults, and can be used as a sedative.

Example prescription: Gouteng San, effective for treating infantile nocturnal crying and so-called epilepsy. Uncaria hooks, Chuan Xiong, Cicada slough, Licorice, Paeoniae Radix Alba. The above five flavors are taken internally as a decoction.

Common Knowledge of Teeth: Questions and Answers (31) 245

— Lin Jianxian

(Question 155) How should we pay attention to our lives?

Answer: The lives of urban people today cannot be as natural and simple as those of the ancients or rural people. All the troubles of human affairs, the temptation of profit, and the erosion of thoughts all have the possibility of weakening our nerves and reducing our health. Dental diseases are particularly common in civilized society, which is not accidental. To achieve the goal of prevention, we must keep our health above the average level and actively improve our daily lives. First, we should prevent and avoid overwork of the body and mind, and always keep our spirits and physical strength abundant. To achieve this, we must avoid irregular life, and both work and rest should be scheduled. All improper entertainment, indulgence, insomnia, starvation, etc., should be strictly prohibited. Second, we should preserve our digestive power and avoid overeating. Each meal should be scheduled, and we should chew slowly and deliberately, without rushing. Third, we should handle everything with an optimistic attitude. Fourth, we should quit smoking and drinking to avoid harming the stomach and brain. Fifth, we should strive for appropriate exercise to achieve physical and mental strength and comfort. Sixth, we should find ways to get more sunlight and fresh air. Sunlight can increase vitamins in the body, which is beneficial to teeth.

(Question 156) Why should we prevent the invasion of diseases?

Answer: All diseases can reduce the body's resistance and indirectly induce dental diseases. Neurasthenia, lung disease, typhoid fever, diabetes, venereal diseases, etc., are easily caused by tooth decay or pyorrhea. We should usually prevent the invasion of diseases. If we unfortunately get a disease, we should treat it quickly and never delay it, so as not to affect the teeth.

(Question 157) Can oral medications damage teeth?

Answer: Many people have tooth problems because they think they have taken too much medicine. In fact, it is not like that. However, oral medications containing mercury, lead, potassium, iodine, iron, etc., often induce stomatitis and periodontitis when taken in large doses, so special attention should be paid.

(Question 158) What else should we pay attention to?

Answer: Local protection of teeth is also very important. Do not let them be hit, and do not use them to bite ropes or hard objects, because if the teeth have cracks, they are easy to decay.

A Brief Discussion on Pulmonary Tuberculosis (93) 246

— Hu Jiayan

Everyone knows the importance of air to people; its achievements in the treatment of this disease have been detailed in the previous chapter. However, it is better to prevent the occurrence of this disease with air, rather than relying on air to treat it. This is a "taking it one step further" approach that everyone should be determined to follow! Speaking of its method, it is very simple, that is, one must spend a long time in fresh air every day. The so-called fresh air refers to places with less dust and coal smoke, and more trees. This is a bit more difficult for people living in cities, but you may as well linger in suburban parks and other places. Even taking a step back, although the air outdoors is not necessarily fresh, it is far better than indoors no matter what; of course, this can be enjoyed every day without any cost!

Sunlight is a major enemy of tubercle bacilli, as detailed above; but its contribution to this disease is by no means limited to this point. It can stimulate body cells, so that physiological functions are enhanced, and indirectly can increase the body's resistance to tubercle bacilli. Usually, glandular tuberculosis and bone tuberculosis, which are easily contracted by children, can sometimes be cured with just sunlight therapy. If we stay in fresh air and are also exposed to sunlight, the increase in the body's resistance will definitely be more significant without a doubt.

There are many people who are prone to catching colds if they stay in fresh air for too long; this is especially true for Chinese people, and it is even completely psychological, resulting in suspicion. This is a great misfortune, and to remedy this deficiency, we can only start with strengthening the skin. The method is: develop the habit of staying outdoors more often, rub the skin with cold water (attached to washing the face and bathing), do not wear too warm clothes, do not keep the bedroom too warm, the room should be open windows, and you should also keep the habit of opening windows when sleeping; all these should be started from childhood, so that they will become a complete habit in the future, and there is no need to worry about it.

Is the nutrition of people's bodies good or bad? It has a great relationship with the prevention of infection. Therefore, to increase the resistance of human tissue, it is necessary to fully supply the raw materials of human vitality, the so-called raw materials, that is, nutritious food. Pulmonary tuberculosis is no exception. Regarding its occurrence, it is sometimes entirely due to malnutrition, so people, in addition to sunlight and air, must not lack one of the three required nutrients: protein, fat, and carbohydrates, and they must be appropriately proportioned. Animal meat and fresh vegetables in terms of food should be included, and milk and eggs, which are rich in nutrition, should also be frequently visited. Here the author has to explain one thing. That is, recently some people have greatly promoted the theory of vegetarian hygiene, and this kind of argument has gained the blind following of many people, and even a foreign doctor has written an article holding this view; this is completely wrong. Taking pulmonary tuberculosis as an example, the protein of its animals is particularly important and cannot be easily lacked. If it is said that meat eaters are prone to suffering from tumors, liver diseases, and hardening of blood vessels due to the necessary materials and toxins in animals; then we might as well say that the causes of common intestinal parasites and dysentery are roughly inseparable from eating vegetables and fruits; but we must never advocate banning vegetarian food, because this is completely "throwing the baby out with the bathwater"; then, the so-called vegetarian hygiene theory, its different value can also be imagined! Therefore, the food that people need, both animal meat and vegetables should be equally emphasized, and mixed (of course, patients with this disease are included), and should not be misled by seemingly correct arguments.

There are many diseases that are very likely to induce pulmonary tuberculosis; therefore, in order to prevent the occurrence of this disease, we should also pay attention to the diseases that induce tuberculosis at the same time. In this respect, the respiratory system is second to none! Like tonsillitis, bronchitis, pertussis, measles, etc. in children, are the most obvious examples; if the occurrence of the above diseases can be prevented, indirectly it can be said that it is adding a layer of defense work to pulmonary tuberculosis! In addition, if there are influenza, pleurisy, swollen lymph glands, hemorrhoids, and anemia, menstrual disorders, indigestion, and other conditions, it is very easy to induce this disease, and of course, strict attention must also be paid to it.

If a reader is willing to part with it, I will offer two copies of Kangjian Magazine and four copies of Tiaoyue Magazine as compensation. Please send the letter to Guo Jiwen, No. 47, Kaiming Lane, Nine Mu Di, Nanshi, This City. Those who arrive later will be returned.

What Should We Give Them? 247

— Xijian

Report: "...Overseas Chinese, concerned about the motherland, have successively organized inspection groups to return to the country for sightseeing. According to information from the Overseas Chinese Affairs Department, the Java Samborondang is also organizing a tourist group, with dozens of people, all of whom have lived overseas for several generations and have never set foot on their national soil..."

At this time of national crisis, when the country is precarious, it is a gratifying thing that some overseas Chinese can successively organize inspection groups and tourist groups to visit this ancient motherland. It is like an old man in his twilight years being able to see his long-lost son returning home. The inner joy is truly indescribable.

Because of the weakness of the country, overseas Chinese are being bullied, expelled, and slaughtered everywhere. However, can the ancient motherland give them a little protection and comfort besides expressing sadness? Now they are visiting the motherland with such enthusiasm, but what can this vast motherland give them! Half of the country has changed color, the enemy is flexing its muscles, and there are scars everywhere, all of which make them disappointed. Besides showing them the tall buildings, modern cars in the city, and some mountains and rivers that have not been plundered, what can be offered to them? At the same time, behind this prosperous city and famous mountains and rivers, there are infinite tragedies, bankruptcies, decline, and human tragedies hidden! They are exploited abroad, living an inhuman life, and it is so disappointing to return to their homeland, how sad should it be?

Overseas Chinese have contributed to the motherland. When Mr. Sun Yat-sen made the revolution, he received a lot of assistance from them. During the heroic resistance against the enemy on January 28th, they also received spiritual and material help. Recently, they have also donated a lot of money to buy airplanes to "save the country through aviation." These are all blood and sweat money they have earned despite all kinds of oppression and insults overseas. But what do we give them? It only gives them a broken and declining impression to take back.

"Poison" and Others 248

— Li Yi

First performance of the Experimental Small Theater

It was really endless joy. When I followed the crowded crowd out of the New Light Grand Theater, I was encouraged by this warm mood. On the way, the topics of conversation with friends could not help but focus on the experimental small theater itself and the three plays performed this time; when I now write to express some opinions, my enthusiasm is rekindled, as if I just stepped out of the theater.

In addition to the three plays performed this time, I originally wanted to say a little bit about my opinions on the small theater itself, such as the repertoire, the theater, etc., but due to the length of this article, I want to leave it to another opportunity to say, so I will not mention it here.

As for the three plays performed this time, I watched "The Proposal" from the upstairs hall. Because it was too far away, I couldn't see it clearly, so I don't want to talk about it. Therefore, we should let the audience know that it is not enough to simply kill an enemy. We should "get to the bottom of the matter" and clearly identify who our current giant enemy is! How can we defeat our enemies?

However, in the current situation of script panic, such works that conform to the mainstream of national defense drama are still rare and valuable. The author has written down a naked portrait of the traitor for us, and also a portrait of a righteous and progressive woman seeking survival under heavy pressure. These two different characters are sent together, which makes us more sympathetic and hateful characters. Moreover, the author, Mr. Zhang Min, is an actual practitioner of the drama movement. Based on his rich experience, there are few wasteful or confusing places in the dialogue, and when the traitor is about to drink poison, the author cleverly uses the suspense that can best grab the audience's emotions, wanting to drink and then stopping, making the audience's emotions tense.

Although most of the actors are newcomers, they are very confident in their personalities. This is a general good feeling. Because they are confident in their personalities, they are very kind and real, as if the people of Northeast China are reporting their experiences to us; moreover, the makeup is very good, so we forget that they are actors performing on stage.

The acting skills of the actors are still lacking in experience because they are "newcomers", but their efforts and seriousness (to put it more appropriately, it can be said that they are empathetic) almost cover up this flaw, especially Shen Yi, who plays the younger sister, and Li Qing, who plays the older brother, are very able to show their stern, strong, and rude and vicious character.

Zhao Dan, Wang Weiyi, Zheng Junli, and Xu Tao played very unimportant soldiers, plainclothes teams, etc. here, washing away the bad habit of the self-proclaimed "stars" who are still amazing. This spirit is very worthy of our praise.

The Qin Player 249

— Tang Jun

On the last day of May, a new family moved in upstairs from us, right next door. There were three of them: a middle-aged man and two girls; the older one was about sixteen or seventeen, and the younger one looked no more than fifteen. They were dressed very flamboyantly, easily making people think they were "of easy virtue." (Note)

One evening, I was taking a walk on the Jin'gang Bridge when I happened to meet Section Chief Fan, who lived in the same alleyway, also watching the night boats on the river. He grabbed me, moved the pipe from his mouth, and said with a smile:

"Do you know what the people next door to you do?"

"How would I know? But judging by appearances, they don't seem like upright people!"

"Let me tell you, I know all about them!" He tapped his pipe on the railing. "That man is a qin player, specifically involved in underhanded dealings. Both girls are his adopted daughters. He abducted the older one from Guanwai, and he got the younger one from a female opera singer, who bought her and gave her to him as a gift. He teaches the two girls to sing Beijing opera, and they're currently performing at the Zhonghua Tea House in the Japanese concession. I often hear them sing there. Last week, I even requested the older girl to sing 'Yu Tang Chun'! Ah, she sings it well! The rhythm is perfect, every beat is precise, clear and crisp, practically no less skilled than Mei Lanfang. If you heard her, your bones would melt! Haha..."

After hearing this, I didn't say a word, staring blankly at the faint shadow of the bridge on the water. A sense of oppression filled my heart, until Section Chief Fan, squeezing his throat, hummed softly, "Chong Laobo says he is wrongly accused and can't defend himself..." and walked across the bridge. Only then did I subconsciously move my feet and slowly saunter back to my dwelling.

It was already past midnight when I went to sleep. Loneliness began to embrace the night. I quietly fell asleep. Not long after, a sound on the stairs startled me awake! The door next door opened; they had returned.

"Dad, you forgot to bring back the erhu."

"You're deliberately trying to cause me trouble! I've suffered and toiled to raise you two, hoping you'd earn enough to feed me in my old age. Who knew you'd want to fly away before your wings were even strong enough! You're delusional! As long as I'm alive, you won't get away with it!"

Then came a burst of sobbing, painfully assailing my heart. I quietly peeked through the crack in the board wall. The man was viciously pinching the older girl's legs and waist, holding scissors in his other hand. I saw the girl kneeling on the ground, tears streaming down her face, begging for mercy. The man's eyes were like a ferocious beast's, the scissors pointed at her chest, as if to say, if you scream, I'll stab you to death! The younger girl was also kneeling beside her, her face covered in blood and tears.

What a cruel and terrifying thing! My heart trembled. I almost cried out. After I lay back in bed, my clothes were soaked with sweat. I felt the cruelty and horror of this world!

"Damn it! You won't know what's what unless I give you some pain!"

"Dad, I... I won't dare again..."

"Who doesn't know that Chen Erye is willing to spend money? He spends thousands upon thousands every year. Any girl he takes a fancy to gets rich and becomes lucky. Others burn incense and pray, hoping for it, but you refuse him, and instead you fool around with that little good-for-nothing, Xiao Lengzi! (Note) If you don't bring Chen Erye back tomorrow, I'll skin you alive!"

People thrown into the filth of life, trampled upon, insulted, harmed, forever sinking into the abyss of pain, bearing the heavy wounds of hunger, without protest, without struggle, their fate destroyed in the darkness! How pitiful they are! I fear that one day they will be murdered!

Not long after they went to sleep, the girl emitted an unbearable moan of pain, clearly being trampled upon by intense, unrestrained bestiality!

Lost in painful thoughts all night, I was furious! I wanted to shout, but I finally endured it.

Early in the morning, the two girls got up and tuned their voices on the platform, their shrill, delicate voices rising and falling, the mournful, resentful tones constantly squeezed from their vocal cords. As the bells of the Hedong Church chimed, the sun was already high in the sky. The qin player got up to wash and rinse his mouth, and only then did they stop tuning their voices and go inside to serve him breakfast. Afterwards, the qin player picked up his old bass erhu, and the two girls took turns practicing singing, over and over. When they missed a beat, the qin player would scold, "What are you thinking about again! You worthless thing!" Naturally, they had to sing again. When they sang to the part "Going out to hunt..." he paced back and forth, scolding, "Damn it! I've told you so many times, that 'hunt' character should be sung lower and lower, until the last note rises, and then you start singing again! And so, the second time, the first time, the..."

After lunch, they dressed neatly and followed him out, not returning until after midnight. Almost every night, I heard the girls' crying and moaning.

Every morning, Section Chief Fan would run up to the third floor to stroll around. When he saw me, he would always say, "The air up here is very good. It's good to exercise here." I knew his "heart wasn't in what he was doing," so I just casually hummed and hawed. Several times I saw him talking to the older girl in secret, when the qin player was still asleep.

Suddenly, one night, the qin player brought the younger girl back alone, and started hitting her as soon as they entered the door. She cried and screamed, and he kept hitting her while forcing her to ask:

"Tell me the truth, where did your sister go? If you don't tell me, I'll kill you!"

"After singing 'Fenhe Bay', she went out, I... don't know..."

He beat the girl half to death, then went out and called the police, who took the girl away. This time I saw the girl's tear-stained, bloodless face.

The next day, Section Chief Fan was gone. I was very suspicious. Later, I asked the teahouse attendant, who said that Section Chief Fan's name was Fan Lengyun, and everyone called him Xiao Lengzi. Only then did I realize that the older girl had eloped with Section Chief Fan.

After living there for a week, the teahouse attendant came to tell me:

"The little girl next door died in the Public Security Bureau."

Note 1: "Of easy virtue" refers to prostitutes. Note 2: "Da mi" means "honey."

Life and Death 250

— Chang Feng

A'cui's due date was approaching, and Zhang, the landlord, had specially sent a sedan chair to welcome her mother to the city. The old woman had just returned from the fields after bringing her husband his meal. From afar, she saw the sedan chair in front of her house, the two sedan carriers fanning their chests with large coolie hats under the tree. The old woman was most afraid of seeing that sedan chair. She would always remember that her daughter A'cui had been carried away in that sedan chair and sent into the mouth of a tiger. Now, it had been over a year, and she had gone to the city twice but had not seen her daughter once. Last year, her husband had gone to the granary to pay rent, and only after begging and pleading did Master Zhang hear his daughter call out "Father" once.

Thinking of A'cui, the old woman's legs felt weak and she couldn't move. The lunch basket in her hand gradually became heavier. Although she thought of detouring back to her own back door from the other side of the field bank, her trembling appearance had already been noticed by the sedan carriers. They ran up from afar, took the lunch basket from her hand, and called her "Old Madam," saying, "Our master is taking Madam to the city. The sedan chair is waiting at the door."

The old woman opened her dazed eyes and looked at the people who came. She had never dreamed that a small-footed old woman would have a day to be called "Madam." But she was not allowed to consider, and the two sedan carriers had already taken her away, carrying her away like her daughter A'cui had been snatched into the sedan chair, flying away.

The old woman felt dizzy and confused, as if she were haunted by ghosts. She didn't know what dangerous things she was about to encounter. She also seemed to recall many things, but those things did not take root in her mind, rising and falling like bubbles. It was only when the sedan chair entered the bustling city that she struggled to shout out:

"Hey! Where are you taking me?"

The sedan carrier in front turned his head and glanced at her, slowing down a little and answering:

"The young mistress is about to give birth, and we are taking Madam to help."

The sedan chair stopped right in front of Zhang, the landlord's house. When the old woman recognized that it was the tiger's mouth—the screen wall painted with the Taiji diagram, the two black lacquered wall doors—she finally understood. Could it be that A'cui was giving birth? This was good news, and her husband would be happy to know. So she subconsciously looked back, but her husband was not following behind. Behind her were the sedan carriers who had hurriedly carried her here.

Two maids helped her enter the door. Having farmed Zhang the landlord's land for over ten years, this was the first time she had entered through the main gate. The high hall, the courtyard, the corridors, all dazzled the old woman's eyes. Now, the hatred she felt for Zhang the landlord had changed: he had not mistreated her daughter A'cui. Zhang the landlord had no sons. If her daughter gave birth to a boy, she would enjoy endless blessings for the rest of her life. Hadn't she already been called "Old Madam"? In that case, her husband would be "Old Master." May Heaven bless them so that they would turn their lives around from farming.

When she reached the earthen room, Zhang the landlord invited her to sit down. The old woman couldn't think of a title to address Zhang the landlord. The words "son-in-law" had already reached her lips, but she didn't dare to say them. She stared at the two-stroke mustache on her son-in-law's lips, and after a long time, she asked vaguely:

"How is A'cui?"

Zhang the landlord was smoking a cigar, as if he hadn't heard her question. After the maid brought tea, he looked at the inner room and said:

"A'cui is about to give birth. If she gives birth to a boy, your good fortune will be great!" Zhang the landlord smiled slightly. He was already over fifty years old and had married five concubines but had not had a child. It was the year before last that the old woman's husband owed rent, and the bailiff, wanting to make extra money, exaggerated and snatched A'cui to be Zhang the landlord's sixth concubine. The landlord did not stay in A'cui's room for two months before abandoning her. It was only when he found out that A'cui was pregnant that he became happy.

The old woman wanted to ask to go into the inner room to see her daughter, but her son-in-law only paced in the room, giving her no chance to speak.

The doctor came out, and Zhang the landlord immediately went up to ask what was wrong. The doctor's face was stiff and lifeless, and he leaned close to Zhang the landlord's ear and said in a low voice: "The young mistress is too young, and the fetus is too large. I'm afraid we'll have to perform surgery, but if we save the mother, we can't save the child, and if we save the child, we can't save the mother."

"Is it, is it impossible to have both?" Zhang the landlord frowned.

The doctor shook his head: "It seems there is no way!"

"Then, save the child!" He decided decisively.

The old woman jumped up suddenly when she heard this. She grabbed the doctor's hand: "Doctor, that won't do! That won't do! Save the mother; my A'cui." She looked at Zhang the landlord: "Landlord Zhang, I beg you, save A'cui! She can have children again. I only have this one daughter. Save the mother!"

A tragic cry came from the inner room. The doctor twisted the old woman's hand, raising his eyebrows to seek Zhang the landlord's consent. Zhang the landlord lowered his head. The doctor immediately went into the inner room, and the door was tightly closed again.

The old woman knelt down in front of Zhang the landlord. She could only shout to save the mother! Save the mother!

Unfinished Writing 251

— Shi Feng

Not particularly short, his facial profile resembled that of Barbusse. I don't know if his real name was Feng Qiangzhi, because I sometimes saw him receive letters with different names, and some friends often called him Old Jiang.

Because he resembled Barbusse a bit, he often seemed quite pleased with himself, showing others his unwritten manuscripts, although his great work was always an "unfinished masterpiece." He said, "Look, I'm about to finish it. It's a novel, very influenced by Gorky." The next day, he might change his tune: "I'm not writing that novel anymore. I'm going to write poetry, really. I've been reading a lot of poetry recently, and my own poetic inspiration has been ignited. I want to use my burning, passionate pen to write down the stories of national heroes and turn them into a great epic poem." Judging by his tone, it was as if he was already standing among millions of readers, receiving their adoration. He lived happily like this every day, in his "unfinished masterpiece," laughing with his low nasal voice.

His friends all adopted an indifferent attitude toward him. "What will he ever accomplish?" That's what everyone thought. Just look at his past actions; he didn't seem like someone who could get anything done. Sometimes I also stood on the same side as my friends, directing cold sarcasm at him, even saying with a mocking tone, "Hey, has your great work been published yet?" He would say with a forced smile, "It's not finished yet."

The one called Bin would interject, "It doesn't matter. I'll publish it for you, and all the money from the sales will be yours..."

"Don't joke around; I'm writing, I'm writing hard!" he would say, laughing with his low nasal voice. Then he would wave his hand at us and walk away with light steps. "Goodbye!" he would shout, waving his hand, as if very embarrassed.

I criticized Bin's words, because such an attitude was not suitable for Old Feng, because he was someone who often needed encouragement from others and was very ambitious. Words that hurt him too much would cause him to lose happy feelings for his friends or himself. For example, when he was writing an article, even if he often abandoned it before finishing, it was our responsibility to help him complete it, and not to determine that he would never write a work. However, Bin was someone who only knew how to joke around; he didn't pay much attention to other things. So he just smiled at my opinion. However, a bad phenomenon finally appeared in Old Feng's behavior. (To be continued)

Radio Program - Radio Play Script

Suzhou People (13) 252

— By Gu Wenzong

Dajun: Ah—may I ask your honorable surname?

Jinghong: My humble surname is Shen.

Dajun: Does Miss Shen have a name card with her? May I have the honor of receiving one?

Jinghong: Certainly. Then may I exchange one with you?

Dajun: That would be even better. (Sound of exchanging name cards, reading name card) Shen Jinghong, Wuxian County, Jiangsu.

Jinghong: Zhao Dajun, a native of Wuxian County, Jiangsu Province, Republic of China—ah! Mr. Zhao is from my hometown?

Dajun: Yes, Miss Shen. Miss Shen's Mandarin is very standard!

Jinghong: Mr. Zhao, you are too kind. My speech is already close to distorted and impure Mandarin. How can it compare to Mr. Zhao's fluent and accurate Mandarin?

Dajun: You are too kind. Since I went to America, I have forgotten most of my Mandarin. I must be mispronouncing many words. Please, Miss Shen, give me some pointers.

Jinghong: There's no need to talk about that. Let's study together.

Liya: Hello, Miss Shen! You're hiding here by yourself? Good, I've been looking for you for a long time!

Jinghong: As soon as I got on the train, I sat here and didn't move. You were looking for me? How could I not know?

Liya: Let's not talk about that now. I'll ask you, have you eaten?

Jinghong: I have.

Liya: What did you eat?

Jinghong: I bought two pieces of bread and two pieces of beef. I hastily counted that as lunch.

Liya: Oh! How can you eat so little? And those things aren't very sanitary! Moreover, those things don't have much nutrition.

Jinghong: Then what kind of sanitary things did you eat?

Liya: I ordered a set meal. The food on this train is very good. I heard that the chef on this train used to be the chef at the British Embassy, so what he makes has a full British flavor. Moreover, it's cheaper than what you can buy at a big hotel, only one dollar per set meal. Why didn't you eat that?

Disliking the Old and Loving the New

Zhang Ping...Chen Rong

Zhang Ping's Wife...Pei Jiu

Boot Seller A...Zhou Ying

Boot Seller B...Jufen

Boot Seller C...Li Lingying

Disliking the old and loving the new is indeed in line with the public's psychology. Knowing full well that something is still usable, but because it is old, it is discarded. Even if you spend money to buy something worse than the old thing, you are still happy with it. Why? Because it is new. Therefore, the value of everything is based on newness as the standard.

Zhang Ping is a practical demonstration of the above point. The boots on his feet are indeed old! But the boots are not damaged in any way. It's just that they have been bought for a long time, so he has the idea of disliking the old and loving the new in his heart. He asks his wife for ten dollars to go out and buy new boots. How could he know that after spending ten dollars and exchanging the boots three times, the result is still the original old boots? And he doesn't even know it, so he happily goes home, thinking that after spending ten dollars and exchanging the boots twice
